Economic Supplement

World Economic Panic and Chinese Currency

— Lecture by Huang Xianzhang, Recorded by Chen Yiru

(1) Causes of the World Economic Panic—

(A) Internal Contradictions of Financial Capitalism: The main reason for this panic is, of course, the problem of the entire system. We must understand that in the current trend of financial capitalism, all efforts are made solely for its own interests: such as how to implement rationalized management? How to improve productivity? In short, the aim is to expand its own profit rate as much as possible. Therefore, under this financial capitalist organization, various industrial sectors engage in frenzied speculative competition, leading to an inability to maintain a balance between production and the general supply and demand of society. On one hand, overproduction is formed; on the other hand, the employed labor force, affected by overproduction, is squeezed out of factories, joining the ranks of the unemployed one by one. The panic of unemployment is spreading universally, forming a common phenomenon within various capitalist countries, circulating continuously without end.

(B) International Contradictions of Financial Capitalism: Due to the progress of production technology and the expansion of capital, the quantity and variety of products have also greatly increased. In the domestic market, they gradually stagnate, inevitably pushing exports outward to seek national prosperity. As a result, everyone tries their best to force exports and restrict imports: market competition is becoming increasingly fierce, and everyone adopts protective trade methods as a necessary means. In the end, everyone uses their national political territory as a boundary, squeezing out foreign goods, not allowing foreign goods to be freely imported, and international tariff wars and quantitative import restrictions arise accordingly. The circulation of goods is thus greatly hindered.

(C) Burden of War Debts and Reparations: After the World War, according to the Treaty of Versailles, Germany, in addition to losing territory and colonial possessions, had to compensate for all the losses suffered by ordinary people in all countries during the war. After several conferences and the formulation of various reparations plans, the so-called "standard year" was finally reached from 1924 to 1928. From then on, Germany had to pay 2.5 billion gold marks in reparations annually. However, Germany, exhausted from the war, how could it afford such a large amount of reparations? At the same time, because most European countries were debtors to the United States, most of Germany's reparations flowed to the United States. However, France received more reparations and paid less debt, so its financial situation was comparatively better than other European countries. As a result, a large amount of gold was concentrated in the United States and France. The following table lists the amount of gold reserves in the United States and France in September 1932 and the amount of gold reserves in various European countries (unit: millions):

United States September 1933: 4,190

France June 1932: 3,200

United Kingdom June 1932: 600

Germany June 1932: 196

Japan June 1932: 115

From the above table, we can see that the amount of gold reserves in the United States and France has reached a very large amount. In the United States and France, there is a panic of gold surplus, while in European countries, there is a lack of gold, resulting in currency tightening and a significant reduction in purchasing power.

(D) Reduction of Imports to Europe and the United States from the Soviet Union, Far Eastern Countries, and Various Colonies:

(1) The Soviet Union used to be an important market for various capitalist countries because it did not have industries as developed as those in advanced European capitalist countries, and almost all industrial manufactured goods relied on the supply from various capitalist countries. The various capitalist countries could transport their surplus goods to this huge, underdeveloped Soviet Union. However, after the success of the First Five-Year Plan, the situation changed drastically, almost unrecognizable compared to the past. The Soviet Union not only did not regard imports from various capitalist countries as necessary, but its own production of various industries sharply entered the market of world imperialism and competed fiercely with it. This is also a major reason for the reduction of European trade exports and the weakening of purchasing power in the Eastern market.

(2) The rural economy of Far Eastern countries, especially China, has suffered from the impact of foreign goods dumping over the years, resulting in extremely low prices for agricultural products. The rural economy will inevitably be exhausted day by day, with no way to recover. No matter how foreign goods flood the market, no matter how hard they try to dump them, there is no way to restore purchasing power. Moreover, most of the Far Eastern countries use silver dollars. After the sudden decline in 1928, due to the relative decline in the exchange rate of silver against gold standard currencies, the general purchasing power was greatly reduced, resulting in a reduction in the foreign exports of various capitalist countries.

2. Countermeasures of Various Countries to the World Economic Panic

The policies of various countries towards the economic panic cannot be exactly the same due to their different specific circumstances, but we can summarize them into the following five items:

A. Reducing production has almost become a common method for various financial capitalist countries. According to a 1932 survey by the German Landscape Research Institute, global production has been reduced by more than 30%.

B. Increasing protectionist tariffs and controlling international trade.

C. Abandoning the gold standard. The United States first banned gold exports and then abandoned the gold standard. The United Kingdom followed in the footsteps of the United States and immediately announced the abandonment of the gold standard, so as to compete with the United States in the international market.

D. Devaluing the currency and inflating the currency: For example, the new currency policy of the United States on January 25th this year. The measures taken by this currency policy are as follows:

(1) Devaluation of the gold dollar by 40% to 50%.

(2) Gold is nationalized, not circulated, and not exchanged.

(3) The surplus gold obtained from devaluation is used to establish an exchange rate stabilization fund of 2 billion gold dollars.

The weight of each gold dollar in the United States was originally 25.8 grains, but now, after deducting 40%, or 940 grains, it becomes 15.237 grains!

The purpose of this policy is to raise prices, relieve debtors, and thereby encourage domestic production recovery, reduce unemployment, and alleviate financial panic.

E. Raising the price of silver (1) The Nine-Power Silver Agreement produced by the London Conference in 1933! Approved on April 1, 1934, and came into effect!! It stipulates that silver-producing countries purchase silver; restricts the sale of silver by silver-holding countries, namely India, Peru, Spain, etc.; restricts India to sell only an average of 35 million ounces of silver in 1934, and the total amount of silver sold within four years must not exceed 140 million ounces; restricts China from selling raw silver obtained from melting currency within four years, etc.

(2) The U.S. Silver Nationalization Policy, namely the Silver Purchase Act of 1934 on August 9, 1934, stipulates: (1) Set the basis for the monetary value of gold and silver at 75% gold. (3) The above silver may be purchased by the state, and the purchase price shall be set at no more than 50 cents per ounce for domestic silver. (4) Control the export or import of currency silver and other transactions. (5) Impose a 5% tax on silver transaction profits. (6) Issue silver certificates with silver as a reserve.

The above two facts, 1 and 2, are both aimed at raising the price of silver, hoping to thereby increase the purchasing power of silver-using countries. Looking at the above five methods, items C, D, and E all focus on the reform of the currency system. French economist Francis Delaisi and American Pittmon are both supporters of items D and E. French Truchy and Millard both opposed them from their own positions. For example, Truchy advocated restoring the original function of gold coins; Millard believed that currency devaluation and inflation are greatly harmful to workers, etc. They either argue from the perspective of their own country's interests or from the perspective of class interests, and we do not need to criticize them one by one. Now, let's talk with you about how currency devaluation in various countries and raising the price of silver affect Chinese currency.

(3) The Impact of Raising the Price of Silver on Chinese Currency

(A) First, in terms of the general economy:

(1) If the price of silver is raised, prices in China will inevitably fall, while in gold standard countries, gold coins will depreciate and prices will rise!!

(2) The exchange rate of Chinese currency will rise, and the exchange rate of foreign currency will fall - that is, forward exchange will rise and reverse exchange will fall!!

(3) Raising the price of silver is conducive to dumping foreign goods and unfavorable to China's exports.

(4) After the price of silver rises, it is unfavorable to international income calculated in gold coins and beneficial to expenditures calculated in gold coins; it is beneficial to income calculated in silver coins and unfavorable to expenditures calculated in silver coins. However, China's tariff revenue will inevitably decrease due to the high price of silver in terms of customs gold; and the remittances of overseas Chinese will also be further reduced due to the high price of silver. However, there are also benefits to raising the price of silver, such as repaying foreign debts, and the expenses of embassies and students can of course also be reduced by a considerable amount of silver coins. However, compared with the amount of imports, this benefit is truly insignificant.

(B) Specifically for China:

(1) China is a silver standard country and the head of the world's silver-using countries. The following table shows the average percentage of silver sales from 1928 to 1932, which shows China's relationship with silver.

Percentage of Sales Occupying Silver Production Percentage of Sales Occupying Silver Supply

China 40% 30%

India 32% 25%

Industry 21% 15%

Coinage 32% 25%

From the above table, we can see that raising the price of silver has a very significant impact on China. In principle, raising the price of silver increases the exchange rate of Chinese currency against foreign currencies, which seems to be very beneficial to China. In fact, this is not the case at all. The reasons are as follows:

(2) After the price of silver rises abroad, China's silver reserves will inevitably flow out. The fact that more than 200 million yuan of Chinese silver coins have flowed out in the past three or four months proves this. The outflow of silver will lead to insufficient currency reserves in China, coupled with the reduction of remittances from overseas Chinese, the country will inevitably lack silver coins and will become a paper money world, which will inevitably lead to financial panic.

(3) Raising the price of silver, due to exchange rate relations, is conducive to the promotion of foreign goods and reduces China's exports, and imports will be even worse. Last year, imports exceeded 700 million yuan, and it is still unknown how it will end this year. Therefore, China's debt is increasing day by day, and it has no choice but to become more dependent on the economy of capitalist countries to survive. In other words, China will inevitably become more colonized.

(4) After the price of silver rises, the price of domestic copper coins will relatively fall, and the lives of ordinary people will be subjected to more severe oppression. Not only will there be a general reduction in purchasing power, but it will also further accelerate the bankruptcy of the rural economy, forming an unmanageable situation.

(4) How to Resolve China's Currency Crisis?

Based on the above-mentioned crisis, domestic people are very concerned about this currency panic problem. The solutions proposed by the general public can be roughly summarized into the following four points:

(A) Banning silver exports. This route is not feasible in China because there are extraterritoriality and foreign banks acting as speculators, and the government has no way to exercise the power of prohibition.

(B) Implementing the gold standard (such as the Kemmerer Plan) is also not feasible because China lacks gold coins.

(C) Levying taxes on silver exports and attaching methods to balance exchange rates. These two policies have been implemented by the government and are still a stopgap measure at the moment.

(D) Reforming the Currency System

(1) Reduce the cash reserve for paper money issuance to 40% in order to relatively inflate the currency.

(2) Improve the silver standard system, so that silver becomes a guarantee means domestically and a circulation means abroad, so that Chinese currency is separated from the world silver price. The method is to stop cashing out without prohibiting silver exports; secondly, adopt the method of "requiring importing merchants to present verification of goods to the central bank and purchase silver in full to offset the price of goods"—

See Zhou Bodi's article "Critique of the US Silver Policy," published in New China, Volume 2, Issue 17—

This is just an ideal, and even if it can be implemented, it may not be able to resolve our currency panic.

Conclusion: China's currency panic is the concrete manifestation of China's economic panic. Imperialism can use economic policies to alleviate its crisis, but China can absolutely not use currency policies to resolve the crisis of economic panic. The reason is:

The currency of rural China flows into cities, from cities into big cities, and then from big cities back into foreign countries, which is a continuous phenomenon. Because China's national capital is restricted by imperialism, and industries cannot develop, there are no adequate exports to offset this year after year of high imports, so a balance can never be achieved in international payments. If this continues, one day the people will be impoverished and the country will be bankrupt, becoming a country without gold and silver. Even if foreign countries transport gold and silver to China by way of investment, it is no different from falling further into the status of a colony, unable to extricate itself forever. Therefore, the current problem in China is that the panic caused by the price of silver is a small matter, and the economic panic caused by capitalist aggression is a big matter. Other countries can use economic policies to solve economic panic; only China must first start with political struggle to achieve the goal of resolving economic panic. There are many methods of political struggle, but at present, we believe that the whole country should have the following consistent common efforts, namely:

(1) Complete a unified and independent country;

(2) Organize a sound and powerful government;

(3) Implement planned economic construction;

(4) Implement a controlled policy of foreign trade.

The Effect of Increased Silver Tax and the Surge in Foreign Exchange Rates

— Zhang Yifan

The silver problem has now almost become a kind of "hot and cold disease" in China's currency system. Everyone feels the suffering of fever and chills, just like malaria patients, from the ups and downs of silver prices. Since April of this year, the continuous and large-scale outflow of silver reserves has made the Chinese people like startled birds. However, the increased export tax and equalization tax on silver have not been as miraculously effective as quinine. Recently, due to the soaring foreign exchange rates, and at the same time, reports in the newspapers have been spreading the news that unscrupulous merchants are still continuing to ship silver out of the country in secret. As a result, everyone is talking about it with fear, and panic-strickenly believing that the reason for the soaring foreign exchange rates is this. The soaring foreign exchange rates are indeed closely related to the extreme tightness of the silver market; and the large-scale export of silver in the past is indeed a major reason for the depletion of the silver market today, so it is indeed reasonable to say that the soaring foreign exchange rates are due to the continued export of silver. However, at present, at least in the current soaring of foreign exchange rates, there does not seem to be much connection between the two. However, the fact that silver can still escape is indeed a manifestation of the weak effect of the tax increase policy. The soaring foreign exchange rates in Shanghai are another matter. Heaven has its own reasons. It seems unnecessary to lump them together.

When the silver tax increase order was promulgated, the tide of silver outflow in Shanghai did seem to stop for a while; at the same time, records of inward movement did appear repeatedly in newspaper reports. As a result, everyone was happily thinking that the tax increase policy really had the effect of quinine, and everyone believed that from then on, silver could come to an end, and the rural finance of the interior could also have the hope of being rescued from its dire straits. In fact, the internal leakage of silver owes little to the power of the tax increase policy. The achievement that the tax increase policy can realistically achieve is, to exaggerate, only to temporarily cause some shocks in the international community, and to reduce the atmosphere of silver price soaring for about three weeks. To be honest, it only makes the open shipment of silver exports turn into secret or tricky shipment exports, and at the same time, at most, it opens another door of increased revenue for the state. What else can be gained?

Everyone knows that the purpose of increasing the export tax and equalization tax on silver is to prevent the domestic outflow of silver reserves, and to avoid the complete bankruptcy of the domestic financial foundation. In fact, how much of the ownership of domestic silver reserves belongs to the Chinese people? At the same time, was there really sufficient legal tender collateral in the domestic financial foundation yesterday? Mr. Yang Yinpu is right to say that the inflow of domestic silver into foreign banks in China is no different from the outflow to London and New York. And the retention of silver in foreign banks in China or its transfer abroad is essentially the same. Fairbank also admitted in a fair manner that the large influx of silver into China in the past could not be regarded as an increase in China's silver base, it was just mostly for maritime "private storage." The extreme tightness of inland finance has fully indicated that China's financial foundation has long been empty. From this point of view, the contribution of the silver tax increase policy to the domestic currency problem was already minimal.

However, some people have said, and the government authorities have also said, that another main purpose of increasing the silver tax and adding the equalization tax is to declare the domestic silver price to be independent from the world silver market. Therefore, let the world silver market run wild, and our domestic silver price can always be hoped to be stable. If the domestic silver price can be stabilized, the commodity prices can be greatly hoped not to collapse again, and the farmers, merchants, and people will no longer suffer. In fact, European and American scholars no longer deeply believe that the terrible drop in prices in their own countries is entirely due to changes in the quantity of currency. Moreover, our country, which has no ability to independently control the price market; this kind of hope can at most be regarded as a kind of pious superstition.

The fact is very obvious that the main reason for the rise in domestic general prices this time - especially the price of staple food - is due to the global disaster this year. The development of military industry is also one of the main functions. Therefore, before the increase in silver tax, the domestic and foreign price markets had already shown this trend. After the tax increase, it happened to coincide with the reduction in autumn harvest results, which was manifested in fact. Due to the general public's concerns about the panic of food, the silver tax increase psychologically caused a temporary tense situation. Therefore, speculators in the exchange took advantage of the situation and created a rare activity in the agricultural product price market recently, and the result of this activity has a real connection with the boiling of the foreign exchange rate this time. The "cessation" of silver outflow and the beginning of internal leakage are also related to this.

The problem needs to be slightly analyzed to reveal the cause and effect.

In recent years, domestic rural areas have gone bankrupt, and cash has been concentrated in cities. At the same time, foreign goods have invaded and sold, and prices have been getting worse every day. Farmers, eager to raise money to make a living and pay off debts, have to harden their hearts and sell their agricultural products at low prices. The agricultural product price market is becoming increasingly depressed. Bankers in the city are suffering from a lack of investment avenues, so they are carrying out capital activities to the countryside in the name of saving the rural areas. In order to ensure the safe collection of their principal and interest, they concentrate on mortgage lending on agricultural products, and a considerable amount of agricultural products flows into the newly established large agricultural product warehouses. However, the pressure of imported agricultural products has not weakened slightly, so the domestic agricultural product market is still stagnant. By the grace of heaven, a drought demon came into the world; harvests in various places were poor, and panic rose suddenly. The prices of agricultural products that had fallen for a long time began to rise. At the same time, food merchants also showed their skills. Taking advantage of the farmers' urgent need for money, they made large purchases when prices rose slightly. I believe that at least three-quarters of the 4 million piculs of rice and grain stored in warehouses across the country today belong to landlords and merchants. Landlords and merchants have more money on hand and do not need to sell urgently; at the same time, because the famine has already formed, everyone is optimistic about the future (that is, the price of rice and grain will skyrocket in the spring when the green and yellow are not connected); therefore, everyone is waiting patiently. The arrival of goods in the Shanghai rice market is rare, and the market price will of course rise again; and precisely because the arrival of goods in the interior is scarce, the flow of funds is also slow. The recent sharp drop in foreign exchange rates is the reason for this. The foreign exchange market is determined by the rise and fall of commercial exchanges. In recent years, all industries have withered, industries have been depressed, and inland agricultural products have warehouses stationed; there is no need to rush to the city immediately. Therefore, the commercial exchanges between the city and the inland are light, and the flow of funds is slow; this has created a record of unprecedented decline in foreign exchange rates since this year. However, the autumn harvest this time is reflected in the sharp reduction in results. Therefore, the Shanghai rice price and miscellaneous grain market, as usual, will inevitably fall sharply under the killing price of unscrupulous merchants during the autumn harvest; but today, due to the above reasons, it still maintains its upward trend. This situation, on the one hand, allows inland landlords and merchants to sell their stored goods and replace them with new rice; in a transition, they can both adjust the current high-price profit first, and still maintain their hope of hoarding and reversing prices in the spring. At the same time, farmers who have been ruined by grain for years, seeing the activity in the market today, are also satisfied, and will transport their newly harvested goods to the city for sale. The rice merchants in the city, looking up with attention, - the landlords and merchants holding the same hope, all ask the question that the rice price is still firm when the autumn harvest is on the market, not to mention when the green and yellow are not connected in the spring, when the price is always soaring? It will inevitably be much larger than today. Why not absorb more spot goods as soon as possible to wait for the arrival of the God of Wealth. Each has its own heart, each has its own ambition, so the commercial relationship between the city and the interior is suddenly frequent. The flow of funds has also suddenly increased. The increase in the amount of bill exchange recently is proof of this. Since this exceptional situation has occurred, and at the moment Shanghai is in the busy financial season. In previous years, Shanghai cash also had the habit of being transferred out in large quantities due to the arrival of inland agricultural products. To sum up these factors, the Shanghai exchange market has greatly improved. According to the market yesterday (the 20th of this month), it has risen to a height of two dimes and two cents. It is a rare record in the past year. But after all, because of the famine, the arrival of goods is still not as large as in previous years, so the degree of commercial frequency and the amount of capital movement are difficult to reach the height of previous years. Therefore, the tension in foreign exchange rates can only be compared with the past two years to show its leap-forward momentum. If compared with the comparison of the 20s, it is still far behind. Today's panicked terror should not be here but in other questions, try to look at the changes in the Shanghai exchange market in the past four years to know.

The highest record of Shanghai's exchange market in the 20th year of the Republic of China was in October. At that time, it had opened a market price of six cents. In the 21st year, the top market time was in February, when the market price had reached seven cents. But then it collapsed; after October, it was pitiful to see that it was at a low of five or six cents. Since last year, it has usually been revolving around the highest one dime and the lowest white loan. Until November, it opened a record of one dime and eight cents; in December, it increased by another two cents to two dimes. However, once it entered this year, the old problem relapsed, and it was not until after August that it began to rise; it had opened a high price of one dime and five cents. It had opened a top market of one dime and six cents in September. But in early October, it returned to small, to be one dime and four cents; this market price of one dime and four cents is already the highest figure in this month. In the middle of the month and below, it has often stopped at six cents. At the beginning of this month, it rose again to one dime and one dime and two cents. It was not until after the 15th that it rose from one dime and three cents and one dime and five cents to one dime and eight cents; on the 19th, it rose to two dimes and one cent; on the 20th, it jumped to two dimes and two cents. It is also said that there are dark markets that make three or four dimes. But it is also said that although there are three or four dimes in the dark market, everyone is still less than trying. This situation does seem to be related to the depletion of the bottom. However, the depletion of the bottom is only the result of the continued outflow of silver; and the soaring of foreign exchange rates cannot be regarded as the result of the depletion of the bottom. However, I am not saying that there is no relationship between the two. I am just saying that the main driving force of the soaring foreign exchange rates this time is the result of the general speculators intensifying their squeeze on the countryside. Otherwise, why was the exchange market far less than it is today during the months of August, September and October when a large amount of silver flowed out? (To be continued)

Commercial News

Financial Foreign Exchange Rates Gradually Get on Track

Yesterday was Sunday, a bank holiday, which caused the foreign exchange market to appear sluggish again. Since the HSBC turmoil subsided, the market price of foreign exchange has gradually gone downstream, and there is a trend of gradually getting on track. Yesterday morning and afternoon, the market price was two dimes and one cent, which was two cents smaller than the previous day. The volume of exchange notes traded was more than 2.8 million in the morning market, and more than 200,000 new transactions. The afternoon market traded more than 500,000, and the small general meeting traded more than 300,000. The foreign collateral loan trading took back more than 900,000, and more than 700,000 new transactions were made. The money house foreign public bill received and solved more than 32.2 million, and the various remittance payments received and solved more than 400,000. Bank receipts and solutions were all at a standstill due to the holiday. Subsidiary currency was firm. The opening price of Jiangnan small foreign currency in the morning market once fell by three yuan, opening at 830 yuan. The afternoon market rose by six yuan due to the strong trading, making 836 yuan. As a result, it was still three yuan better than the previous day. The morning market made no transaction, and the afternoon market made 11,000 angles. The morning market of Guangdong small foreign currency made 770 yuan, which was already four yuan higher than the previous day. Unexpectedly, the afternoon market added another three yuan and five corners, making 773 yuan and five corners. As a result, it was seven yuan and five corners higher than the previous day. The morning market made 180,000 angles, and the afternoon market made 100,000 angles. The copper coin situation also improved, making 290,000 texts, which was 2,000 texts higher than the previous day. The trading volume was 28,130 strings of texts, which was equivalent to 9,700 yuan.

Securities The Bond Market Has Been Hovering for a Week

From December 3rd to 8th last week, the Chinese Business Securities Exchange was about to open the Fifth Plenary Session, that is, the more hope it had, the closer it got, and the market became brewing and hovering. The highest degree of foreign exchange has passed, and there is a trend of gradual decline. People's hearts are unanimously optimistic, and those who do more are very enthusiastic. However, because the silver market is still very tight, comparing the foreign exchange interest rate with the public bond interest rate,

it is still unprofitable. Therefore, those who do more have bought forward contracts one after another to avoid the crush of this month. The congestion of forward bulls is now in a deformed state where the forward and spot market prices are equal, and the hedge remains unchanged. The fundamental reason is still the tight silver market. The environmental situation is actually better than before. If it were not for the silver market relationship, the market price would have soared long ago. Recently, due to rumors, it has turned tired slightly. Current Situation of Tangshan Sanitary Facilities (Part 1)

— Deng Licheng

Medicine is the crystallization of science. With the evolution of science and the progress of society, it is constantly changing and gradually becoming refined. Therefore, its object is not only individual medical cases; the health of the entire society is its purpose. In today's developed health undertakings, medicine has shifted from passive disease treatment to active prevention, which is of great significance to the civilization, prosperity, strength of the entire nation, and the soundness of society. In recent years, China's health undertakings are budding, and civil medical and health facilities are particularly needed. I hereby present a compilation of my on-site investigation of the rural health conditions in Tangshan last month to satisfy the concerns of colleagues regarding China's health undertakings.

Tangshan is a town under the jurisdiction of Jiangning County, located sixty li outside Zhongshan Gate in Nanjing, at a crucial point on the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway. It is famous for its hot springs. With convenient transportation and excellent scenery, it is one of the famous scenic areas of the capital. It has a population of more than 20,000, scattered in more than 50 villages. There were no medical facilities in the town, and people lacked health knowledge, so they were at a loss during epidemics. In view of this, the National Health Administration established a health office in the town in the winter of the 20th year of the Republic of China to popularize medicine among the people and implement rural health. For the convenience of implementation, sixteen villages in the town were designated as rural health experimental areas to gradually promote it. At the beginning of the establishment of the health office, it only provided outpatient services. However, within a few months, it was crowded with patients and the work was busy. In order to expand, four flat houses were built in the west of the town in February of the following year, covering an area of more than four acres. It was completed in July, and the clinic was moved to the new site, expanding outpatient services and adding the following health works: (School health, maternal and child health, environmental health, disease prevention, health promotion, vital statistics. The organization, equipment, personnel, and work overview of the office are described below:

(1) Organization: The health office is directly under the jurisdiction of the National Health Administration and the Health Experiment Office of the National Economic Committee. This spring, Jiangning Autonomous Experimental County joined the cooperation, so it is also the Tangshan Health Center of Jiangning Autonomous Experimental County. However, the funding is provided by the National Health Administration.

(2) Personnel: One chief physician is responsible for medical affairs and designing various health works and other administrative affairs. One midwife is responsible for midwifery and prenatal and postnatal family visits and other maternal and child health works. Three public health nurses are responsible for outpatient patients, mobile medical care, and school health nurse work. In addition, there are two assistant staff members and three male and female workers.

(3) Equipment: (1) Examination room

(2) Pharmacy

(3) Dressing change room

(4) Outpatient waiting room

(5) Minor surgery room for outpatient prenatal examinations and other minor surgeries.

(6) Office for physicians, nurses, and midwives to work outside of outpatient hours.

(7) Exhibition room for displaying various health specimens, maternal and child health posters, health habit posters, children's health toys, etc., for public visits, and mother's meetings, children's meeting venues.

(4) Work Overview:

"A" Disease Treatment:

A. Outpatient Clinic: The outpatient hours are from 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM. Regardless of whether it is sunny or rainy, there are more than 50 to 60 outpatient patients every day, most of whom suffer from gastrointestinal diseases, trachoma, acute conjunctivitis, skin diseases, minor surgery, and malaria. The initial consultation fee is only ten copper coins, and the follow-up consultation fee is five copper coins. Other medicines and surgical materials are free of charge. In addition, in February this year, there was an epidemic of epidemic meningitis in Shidi Village in the town, and more than 60 people were infected at one time. The health center opened a temporary ward for accommodation. At that time, more than 50 people were treated and fully recovered. The treatment method also involved injecting meningitis serum into the spinal cord.

B. Mobile Medical Care: In addition to outpatient disease treatment, one public health nurse is responsible for mobile medical care in villages far from the town every afternoon. The diseases treated are limited to skin diseases, trachoma, malaria, and surgical dressing changes. The medicines carried are mostly a few commonly used daily medicines. In case of critically ill patients, they should be sent to the health center for treatment immediately. I personally visited the mobile medical work with the nurse of the health center and felt that it was very necessary and valuable. Because most farmers are too busy with farming and are often unwilling to come to the health center for treatment for minor illnesses, resulting in serious illnesses. Mobile medical care meets the needs of farmers and achieves the greatest effect on health work.

The Pathological Relationship between Teeth and Eyes in Oral Infections

— Chen Ren

What is an oral infection? Oral infection comes from the English word "Focal infection". This name comes from the United States, because in recent years, research on pathological causes has discovered many systemic diseases, the cause of which is local pathology in the body, such as the teeth in the oral cavity, tonsils, or paranasal sinuses. The chronic pyogenic inflammation that occurs locally here does not present significant local symptoms, so everyone ignores it. However, this is a manufacturing site for toxic bacteria. From here, the toxic bacteria are distributed throughout the body, or other parts of the body, forming systemic diseases, such as toxemia, septicemia, or diseases in other parts of the body, such as kidney, myocarditis, endophthalmitis, etc. American doctors collectively call these infections caused by teeth, tonsils, or paranasal sinuses in the oral cavity Focal infection. Our translation of it as oral infection seems too narrow, as it also includes the paranasal sinuses.

We have many internal eye diseases, such as iridocyclitis, choroiditis, papillitis, glaucoma, etc., which are mostly metastatic. The paranasal sinuses and tonsils of the mouth occupy an important position as the source of metastasis, which doctors know. In recent years, after the discovery of dentogenic focal infection, ophthalmologists have also paid attention to teeth as the cause of metastatic internal eye diseases. At the same time, the close pathological relationship between teeth and eyes was also discovered. According to recent statistics, especially iridocyclitis, the infection from teeth also accounts for 1.2%.

If fashion is the nature of us humans, this phenomenon often occurs in the scientific community. For example, when a new theory comes out, it is often excessively promoted. After the theory that the cause of internal eye diseases is dental infection was announced, it was also highly valued and observed by scholars in general. We do not deny the theory of dental infection, and we admit that dental infection is very likely, because many metastatic eye diseases can be transferred from other places, such as the paranasal sinuses, so why can't they be caused by dental infection? However, the establishment of a theory cannot depend on its possibility, but must have its necessity. We cannot say that dental infection is possible; we must prove that dental infection is indeed a fact. The confirmation of this fact is the proof of this necessity, which is the basis for the establishment of this theory. In seeking the confirmation of necessity, we must also pay attention to what kind of dental disease is the cause of dental infection, and its relationship with eye diseases, so that we can obtain a correct statistical number from the theory of necessity. Based on this principle, we will examine and expand the theory of dental infection.

(2) To prove the necessity of a medical theory, two facts are required: (1) clinical experience, (2) animal experiments. So far, there have been no animal experiments on the theory of dental infection, because there is no experimental method, so there is no way to experiment. The theory of dental infection is entirely based on clinical experience. Now let us first investigate the clinical facts. For example, we have discovered an internal eye disease, and we should devote all our efforts to investigating the cause. Systemic examination and laboratory examination, we have not found any pathology. When we examine their oral cavity, we find that their teeth are not healthy. Can we admit the causal relationship between these two accidental, parallel facts? No! Absolutely not! Even if the number of such coincidences increases, even if we find that everyone with internal eye diseases has unhealthy teeth; at this time, we still cannot admit their absolute causal relationship. Because according to recent reports from dentistry, dental diseases can be said to be a civilization disease, which almost everyone in the city has. However, these dental disease sufferers do not all develop symptoms of dental infection. In large dental hospitals, there are thousands of dental patients and various dental disease sufferers every year, but no eye diseases have been seen. We go further and ask dentists to cure the teeth of internal eye disease sufferers and dental disease sufferers. If the internal eye disease is also cured as a result, then the necessity of this dental infection seems to be proven! Indeed, modern dental infection theory has statistics, all based on this principle. However, we must have a considerable certainty about the concept of "cure." Many internal eye diseases, especially iritis, are often prone to recurrence, and his recovery sometimes occurs suddenly and unexpectedly. Moreover, the extraction of the affected tooth, due to the bleeding of the wound and the decomposition of protein, causes a kind of stimulating treatment method, which often causes the disease to change and heal. Then, this treatment of dental disease and the cure of eye disease are all accidental, or non-specialized causal relationships, so we must observe secondary internal eye disease sufferers who are cured after dental disease treatment for one or two years or more to see if they will recur. If recurrence is still inevitable, then the original cause has not been removed and the root has not been cut off. The cure of this dental disease and the cure of internal eye disease are all accidental, not dental infection. On the contrary, after the dental disease is removed; the cause is eliminated, and the root is cut off, then there will be no recurrence, and the necessity of dental infection can be confirmed.

Only by such accurate clinical report summarization can a correct statistical number be obtained. However, when reviewing modern dental infection presidential reports, it is not noted or detailed whether there is an observation of more than one year on the point of sleep disease cure, and whether the patients in the statistics have no recurrence phenomenon at all.

(2) What kind of dental disease, or where the dental disease can cause dental infection? Researchers are sparing no effort. The route of dental infection is nothing more than metastasis through blood vessels or nerves. Therefore, external dental diseases that do not have a direct contact relationship with blood vessels and nerves have no possibility of metastasis at all.

Page 16

On the contrary, all chronic apical periodontitis, such as granuloma or cyst, which have a close relationship with blood vessels and nerves, are the key to dental infection. The discovery of these apical periodontitis must be done with X-ray fluoroscopy. Therefore, for internal eye diseases suspected of dental infection, X-ray fluoroscopy is an indispensable examination. As for periodontitis, because the pus has an exit, the possibility of its metastasis is naturally reduced, so scholars generally do not admit that it has dental infectivity. Simple caries that have not yet damaged the pulp also have no possibility of infection. If the caries have reached the pulp, then it is in direct contact with blood vessels and nerves, and there is a possibility of dental infection.

Since dental disease and dental infection have such a relationship, more attention should be paid to the statistical reports. So far, no record has been made of what kind of dental disease in all statistical reports. Does the so-called dental disease specifically refer to dental diseases that have the possibility of dental infection? Or all dental diseases? It is not possible to know for sure, so the statistical number is also unable to have scientific certainty.

The location of dental disease and dental infection of internal eye disease is also valuable. Is the relationship between dental disease of the upper jaw and eye disease closer than that of the lower jaw? Does dental disease on the left only have an infectious relationship with the left eye? These issues have not been noticed so far, so there are no detailed records in the statistics.

Since these two steps have not been effectively resolved, the theory of dental infection is still possible, not a necessary theory. Therefore, his statistical number is naturally not accurate. It is still necessary to unite countless ophthalmologists, internists, and dentists to jointly be responsible, jointly research, and jointly collect materials. Only in countless correct, detailed, and scientific materials, that is, in clinical experience, can a correct foundation for dental infection and a true statistical number be created.

Since joint research has a common goal, it must have a common method. I respectfully propose three chapters of the research charter, and please pay attention to them:

(1) Every internal eye disease sufferer must seek a detailed systemic examination, and X-ray fluoroscopy of the lungs is extremely important. At the same time, a dental examination must be done, and X-rays are also necessary.

(2) When a dentist encounters chronic apical periodontitis and other dental diseases that have the possibility of dental infection, they should ask if they have eye diseases or other internal diseases. It is best to ask experts to examine them in detail.

(3) Published records must be detailed. In particular, the records on teeth, such as the location of dental disease, the division of upper, lower, left, and right, what tooth and what disease, and the method of treatment, the more detailed the better, so that the theoretical confirmation is correct and has evidence.

The completion of this article owes much to the discussion with my friend Dr. Gu Hailing (Director of Medical Affairs of the Pediatric Dentistry Hospital). When I started the first draft, Dr. Gu happened to be ill. Dr. Gu's health was so good that he didn't care about it. Who knew that he would die after one illness, and passed away on November 11. I mourn the loss of my friend, and even more mourn the loss of a pillar of the new medical community that is under construction. I rushed to complete this article and respectfully dedicate it to the spirit of Dr. Gu, and silently pray that his spirit of serving the new medicine will never die!

Common Sense Q&A on Diseases

— Cheng Hanzhang

(47) Intestinal Cancer

(Question) Is cancer in the intestine like cancer in other parts of the body, mostly affecting the elderly?

(Answer) Yes. Men over the age of forty are the most affected.

(Question) Where does intestinal cancer occur in the intestine?

(Answer) It occurs most often in the rectum; less often in the large and small intestines.

(Question) When do symptoms of rectal cancer begin to appear?

(Answer) There are no symptoms at the beginning; symptoms only begin to appear after two or three years. However, in young people with special constitutions, it progresses very quickly.

(Question) How does a patient with rectal cancer feel uncomfortable?

(Answer) At first, they often discharge mucus stools; which contain a small amount of blood; later, diarrhea occurs, and there is tenesmus. The sacrum has pressure, or the abdomen is full.

(Question) What are the symptoms if a patient with rectal cancer develops an ulcer?

(Answer) This is caused by friction of the feces causing ulceration of the mucous membrane. At this time, the mucus increases, accompanied by blood, and the urge to defecate is frequent.

(Question) Does the rectum become narrow? What are the symptoms?

(Answer) Cancerous tumors tend to harden and narrow the rectum. At this time, stubborn constipation occurs, and the feces form granules like rabbit feces. There is a feeling of pressure in the sacrum and a feeling of fullness in the abdomen, and there is a dull pain. Sometimes, symptoms of intestinal obstruction occur, or diarrhea and constipation alternate.

(Question) Is there any danger after ulceration or stenosis symptoms appear?

(Answer) The patient becomes acutely weak, or has symptoms of chronic sepsis.

(Question) What is the impact on the bladder and abdominal cavity?

(Answer) Rectal cancer can perforate into these parts and cause major bleeding. Very dangerous.

(Question) Where does colon cancer usually occur?

(Answer) It mostly occurs in the sigmoid part of the lowest segment of the colon. Second, in the cecum of the initial segment of the colon.

(Question) Does a person with colon cancer feel pain in the affected area?

(Answer) In the early stage, they feel almost nothing. When stenosis occurs, the intestinal tube above the stenosis is hyperactive, causing persistent colic.

(Question) What is the stool condition after colon cancer occurs?

(Answer) Mostly constipation, especially if stenosis occurs in the lower part of the colon, rabbit feces or strangulated feces will appear. If the colon cancer is in the upper part, diarrhea and constipation will alternate.

(Question) Does the patient vomit?

(Answer) If the stenosis is in the upper part, the intestinal contents will stay sooner or later. Acute intestinal obstruction occurs, leading to fecal vomiting.

(Question) Where does small intestinal cancer occur in the intestine?

(Answer) It is most common in the duodenum. But small intestinal cancer itself accounts for the least number of intestinal cancers. At this time, jaundice or diabetes may be caused by the pressure of the tumor. If it is in the jejunum, stenosis symptoms will occur, and there will be vomiting.

(Question) What is the treatment for intestinal cancer?

(Answer) There is no other way except early surgical resection. Radium therapy is just a comforting treatment and has little effect.

Common Sense on Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene

— Tang Renjin

(27) Real Fuli (commonly known as Diphtheria)

(2) Laryngeal Real Fuli Kehlkopfdjphtherie

Laryngeal Real Fuli is also known as Laryngeal Glub Kehlkopfkronp. It mostly follows Pharyngeal Real Fuli. It is the most severe and dangerous of the three types of Real Fuli. Children between the ages of two and seven are most likely to suffer from this type of Real Fuli. His main symptom is acute laryngeal stenosis. They are often in danger of life. This is because when suffering from laryngeal Real Fuli, the surface of the vocal cords is covered with fibrinous deposits (pseudomembrane). As a result, the entrance to the airway (glottis) is narrowed. Once the larynx is narrowed, it will cause difficulty breathing. If the difficulty in breathing reaches a high level, it is easy to suffocate and fall into a dangerous state. (To describe this danger in vulgar language, it is holding your breath). I will now briefly explain the process of laryngeal stenosis and its results. Readers and gentlemen, perhaps you can understand it more clearly.

At the beginning of laryngeal stenosis, hoarseness is felt. Glub cough occurs. This cough is an irritating cough. The sound is like a dog barking. An experienced doctor can infer from the sound that it is this disease. If the degree of stenosis increases further, dyspnea will occur. At this time, the pharynx is mostly also red and swollen. But the pseudomembrane does not necessarily have to be seen. The lymph nodes below and behind the mandible are painfully swollen. If a laryngoscope is used to examine the larynx, a grayish-white pseudomembrane is seen attached to the vocal cords and its surroundings. The swelling of the part is obvious, so the flow of air is of course obstructed. Although the body temperature rises, it is not necessary. It rarely exceeds 39 degrees Celsius. The pulse is significantly thin and rapid, and is often irregular. At this time, if a definitive diagnosis can be made early and appropriate treatment is given, it can usually be cured in a few days. Otherwise, if the opportunity for treatment is missed, various symptoms will proceed in order. The air passing through the glottis is more obstructed. Glub cough is also more severe. Dyspnea also reaches its extreme. The carbon dioxide in the blood increases, while the oxygen decreases. Therefore, the skin of the lips, tongue, cheeks, auricles, fingers, etc. loses the healthy skin's redness and turns lead-gray or purple. The patient's face shows an expression of pain. They move restlessly and toss and turn on the bed. The heart is also significantly weakened, and eventually they die of suffocation without rescue. Furthermore, the attack of Glub often occurs at night. It suddenly breaks through sleep and causes difficulty breathing. It suddenly falls into a state of suffocation. This is because the proliferation of Glub-like pseudomembrane during sleep covers the glottis and causes Glub. Sometimes, it can also cause the attack of Glub due to the accumulation of mucus or the adhesion of the edges of the vocal cords on both sides. However, the child can often eliminate this attack by spitting out the fibrinous pseudomembrane. This is nothing more than the glottis accidentally getting a chance to circulate air after spitting it out.

Looking at the process we have described above, the duration of laryngeal Real Fuli is often only one to three days. A week or so is rare. As for a long duration, that is an exception. His cause of death is mostly due to the result of suffocation caused by laryngeal stenosis. This is already a very clear fact. It is not necessary to mention it again.

The most common complications of laryngeal Real Fuli are tracheitis and tracheobronchial pneumonia.

Common Fever Treatment Methods (11)

— Li Xing

If, after an illness, the body temperature is consistently lower than when healthy, for example, a body temperature of 97 degrees (or 37 degrees Celsius), one should delay returning to work. Furthermore, if the heartbeat becomes rapid after minimal exertion following an illness, this also indicates a need for a longer recovery period. One should continue to rest until fully recovered.

As one gradually recovers and reaches the point of being able to get out of bed, one should do so gradually, and not suddenly get up and walk around. If the fever was severe and the illness lasted for a long time, one should be especially careful and take it slowly when getting up. After a prolonged and serious illness, if the legs are weak, the first step is to gradually move the legs while still in bed. The method is to place a pillow at the foot of the bed and use the feet to push against the pillow as an exercise. Gradually doing this will strengthen the legs when getting out of bed. It is not advisable for a patient who has been bedridden for a long time to suddenly get out of bed. The first step is to sit up in bed with the back supported. Initially, sitting up in bed should be for a short period, once or twice a day is sufficient, and gradually increase the number of times and the length of time, as long as the patient does not feel tired. Further progress can be made by helping the patient sit in a chair, for a maximum of five minutes each time. Once in the morning and once in the evening is sufficient. The daily sitting time can be doubled in this way. After doing this for several days, one can help the patient walk around. When gradually moving around after an illness, it is essential to prevent the patient from fainting. Fainting is most likely to occur when the patient gets up quickly to relieve themselves. One should gradually acclimatize to excessively cold or hot environments after an illness. If financially feasible, taking a vacation for several weeks or months after an illness is also worthwhile.

Diet After an Illness As the patient gradually recovers, their appetite will also improve day by day. Be careful at this time not to let them eat too much or eat food that is difficult to digest. Do not base the diet on their appetite, but on the strength of their body. Therefore, it is crucial to avoid rushing to banquets or large meals immediately after recovery. Even the food that healthy people eat regularly should be avoided, and one should eat food that is particularly easy to digest. The most common mistake is to give patients food that they cannot digest or too much food that exceeds their digestive capacity. Indigestion caused by unsuitable food after an illness will hinder a quick recovery to health.

Tonics After an Illness A patient's body is naturally exhausted, anemic, and weak after an illness. Iron supplements to replenish blood, such as Blaud's pills, ferrous citrate, arsenic preparations, strychnine preparations, etc., are appropriate to take together with a suitable nourishing diet. By paying attention to personal hygiene and getting plenty of fresh air and sunlight, recovery to health can be expected soon.

Practical Treatment Methods

The various treatment methods for fever have been described in detail previously. Although the methods are available, the various fever conditions differ, and the treatment must be appropriate for each case. Here, the most notable types of fever illnesses are listed with a general treatment outline for reference by families.

(1) Typhoid Fever Typhoid fever is the most severe and aggressive of the fever illnesses. Hundreds of thousands of people die from this disease in our country every year. The formal period of high fever in typhoid lasts for about four weeks, and the entire fever lasts for more than a month and a half. Improper treatment is truly unspeakably dangerous. With improper treatment, at least three out of ten patients will die. Even with the latest treatment methods, at least ten percent will still die. This is truly a terrible disease. There is still no method to immediately cure typhoid fever completely, but treatment can reduce many of the dangers. The responsibility for treatment lies partly with the doctor and partly with the family. The family's responsibility is to implement the treatment methods prescribed by the doctor. Be sure to prevent the transmission of typhoid fever to others. Implement the prevention methods prescribed by the doctor. A brief description of several important treatments for typhoid fever is provided below.

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (32)

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 8 Clinical Examination Methods

C. Examination of Tubercle Bacilli This is the most important aspect of sputum examination. In the entire diagnosis of pulmonary tuberculosis, there is nothing more accurate and important than the discovery of tubercle bacilli. Their shape and size have already been described in the first chapter, so it can be omitted here. In the sputum of patients with this disease, they are very numerous, especially in purulent sputum; this should be given special attention when collecting sputum for examination. During the examination, a staining procedure is required to clearly distinguish them from the various other components of the sputum; unlike elastic fibers and lung flukes, which can be recognized simply by placing them under a microscope. In ordinary staining, tubercle bacilli appear red, while everything else in the specimen is blue, making it easy to distinguish. If tubercle bacilli are found in the specimen, it is best to further investigate their quantity, commonly categorized into four levels: very few, few, many, and very many; this is naturally sufficient to indicate a general idea. The most accurate comparison involves dividing the quantity in one specimen into ten levels: the fewest being one to four bacilli in the entire specimen, gradually increasing to a few fields with only one bacillus, then one bacillus in one field, further increasing to several bacilli in one field, and so on until extremely numerous. This naturally requires a complete examination of the specimen. The more tubercle bacilli there are in the sputum over several months, the more severe the condition is, and the prognosis is also more dangerous; but this is not always the case, and there are sometimes exceptions.

Many people with this disease do not have tubercle bacilli in their sputum, which is the closed type of the disease mentioned earlier. Even if the sputum contains tubercle bacilli, the results may be greatly disappointing due to improper sputum collection or slight negligence in the staining procedure. Therefore, it is necessary to repeatedly examine several times to determine their presence or absence; hastily concluding that it is not this disease based on a single negative result is even more biased and will be ridiculed by experts.
